Family size ketchup, family size cereal, family size chicken, beef, everything! <Response>None</Response>< Review>
Great little retro gaming shop with a good variety of your main systems. NES, SNES, PS1,2 and 3, GENESIS, some Famicom and some SuperFamicom games too? I think I saw some Master System and Dreamcast in there too definitely more but I found what I was looking for :). Prices are pretty reasonable considering what basic titles go for on the webs so if you got that gaming itch and you live locally, this is a good spot.</Review>

<gmap_id>0x808580ebb2e72f45:0x7aa45a7a3f5e7314< /gmap_id>< Review>
Magic Kingdom is a perfect room for newer players. We plan on bringing our 10 and 6 year olds back to do this room. The path is clear for what you want to do, but the puzzles aren't so easy that you quickly figure out how to accomplish each goal. Having that kind of clarity helped  newer players enjoy and not get too frustrated. It is technologically and visually very well done, and probably my favorite of the dozen or so rooms I have done. Everyone should experience this room.<//Review>

Lots of fun for groups, especially if you have 11 and can take the entire slot. We did a company team event in the Escape the Jail theme and came so close to solving all the puzzles and escaping. <user_name>J. E.< /user_name><Date>1502853875137< /Date><Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
While passing through the Nevada City area I happened upon this cozy store and was delighted by what I found; an extensive selection of fermentation equipment, hops, grains, and spices (including Palo Santo, which reminds me of the streets of La Paz, and I'm excited to experiment with in beer).

I happily found great stainless steel ball valves I had trouble finding elsewhere; staff-member Zack not only gave me the low-down on why easily sanitize-able and temperature tolerant silicon tubing is the way to go and what to consider when purchasing beer faucets, but also shared some tips on his latest simcoe single-hop IPA.

I made 2 trips during my short time there and would definitely recommend it to anyone travelling within an hour of Grass Valley.<//review>

<username>Richard Zapata<//username><Resp>None</Resp><Date>1549406359695<//Date>< review>
I used to drive by this place and would occasionally see a line outside the door. I finally decide to stop in and see what the fuss was about.
Besides the place being a bit small, the food is really what the line is about! Everything I've had has so much flavor and is so good!
They do not skimp on the portions (see the photos to better understand) and I think the prices are pretty good for the portions. I've tried the Super Burritos and I rarely finish them in one sitting. I've also had the Super Nachos with meat and they make a good leftover meal as well. I have not yet tried it but they also serve Menudo on the weekends (maybe Sundays only).
They have a pretty good menu size as well as serving breakfast meals. there are so many things I want to try still!
Now my only complaint is the salsa bar. First, there are no signs to tell you which is which or the hotness of each one. Second, the mild salsa doesn't always look or taste fresh. I tend to stay away from the salsa bar unless it is early in the day and I can be reasonable sure it is fresh. Other than that, I still return and I've always satisfied!<//review>

<text>I will always try and rate this place 5 stars when I can. I've been going here all my life. Since when I could start eating beans (most babies would eat apple sauce!) So about 26 years I've been coming here. Lately, the last couple times tho...I understand people come and go staff wise, you have to stay on top with the cost of living but plates are getting up there in price! < name>
Charles Bartlett< /name>
< date>
1518653768273</date>
<Rating>3< /Rating>< Review>
Good Pho requires rice noodles. That is not what you will get at PHO Noodle House. They use a much thicker flour noodle which is just a mess to eat with chopsticks.

Chicken is probably a safe bet, but I would avoid the beef and pork meat choices. The Spicy Beef includes pork cuts that I've never seen in my life. They looked like half circles of bologna maybe? The beef was definitely not lean.

Nice lunch time atmosphere and service was pleasant. Although I ran into problems with the order and correcting it was a bit of a challenge.

I may go back. But I'm spoiled when it comes to Pho. Hong Kee & Kim in San Francisco is the same price and a big step up in quality. Why a Pho restaurant would use flour noodles instead of rice noodles is beyond me.<//Review>

<review>Delicious pho.

I currently work in the plaza so I frequent the restaurants pretty often. Obviously this plaza is terrible. With the homeless people and all the ricers showing off, it's not pretty. Fortunately the Vietnamese food here is actually the best in Vallejo.

Eating pho twice a week these past four years away in college, I was looking for a good Vietnamese place near home. Pho1 isn't a place to really impress anyone. Vietnamese restaurants just aren't meant for that. Instead it's a real cozy down to earth restaurant with good quality pho. I love the seafood pho they have. I hardly ever see seafood pho in Vietnamese restaurants so try it out if you like a rich garlicky seafood taste.<//review>< Pics>

<user>106341489896640689950< /user><Name>E A< /Name><Time>1375475633888</Time><Rate>4<//Rate><review>PHO SHO!

Sorry, I had to get that stupid, bordering on asian teeny booper-ish misnomer out of my head before I got started on this review. Now that I have that out of the way, on to the review.

Pho (which is pronounced "fa", which also explains the phrase I mentioned at the onset of this review) is one of my favorite soups. Probably number 3 in the list of my favorite soups. My list goes like this:

1. Ramen
2. Udon
3. Pho
4. That junky oh-so bad for you Campbell's one with the mini burgers
5. Dinner cereal

Pho is awesome. Especially on a cold day where you've got a cold and your girlfriend is giving you the cold shoulder while you listen to Stone Cold Steve Austin's theme song. When you think of good quality food, you don't usually think of Vallejo, CA (aka the neglected child of the Bay Area that learned to fend for himself without parental supervision, but strictly on it's steel will and heart of frickin' GOLD.) You're... right for the most part. It's mostly fast food joints and your dime a dozen Chinese restaurants here. But here and there, peppered amongst the landscape, you'll find some good eats. Pho #1 happens to be one of those places.

This little gem is nestled nearby CVS (also the same plaza that houses Starbread aka home of the senorita sweet bread aka crack bread as well as Tapioca Express aka bored young Filipinos wanna hang out in Vallejo and OMG THIS PLACE HAS BOBA! (their wording, not mine)). It's extremely unassuming and you'd never see it driving down Sonoma Blvd. Once you drive into the plaza, you're golden. I know that Burger King is staring at you longingly, but ignore that for now. You're here for some good Vietnamese food.

Inside, the surroundings/environs aren't much to talk about. Just some very basic tables and chairs in here. It's not that big of a place either, though i've seen some pretty nice sized groups eat here before (myself being a part of one of those groups on one occassion.) You'll be handed a menu with ohhhhhhhhhhh so many things to choose from, descriptions and photos a-plenty. Ordering is done is a timely fashion as well. In a few minutes, boom, hot food is on your table.

Everything here is good. The rolls (both the rice noodle ones and fried) are a great way to start a meal here. Just the right amount of tasty nomage. The rice plates are pretty much the bomb. My favorite rice plate is the standard BBQ pork with the egg. I always order an extra egg as I LOVE FRIED EGGS. And there is just wayyy too many good soups to choose from. My favorite would probably be the beef combination one with the beef ball, steak, flank, and tripe. Chicken and seafood soups are also no slouches here. The flavors here are always off the wall and you always get large hearty portions. Leaving here hungry means either a) you didn't order food or b) you are, in fact, the cyborgs that the Conner family tried to warm me about. That and something about a Skynet.

If you're in Vallejo for some reason or another (I can only assume you have family here OR you're visiting Six Flags) and you're craving some really good Vietnamese food, do yourself a huge favor and go to Pho #1. You will leave full and satisfied, the top two things on your meal experience list... which goes like this:

1. Full
2. Satisfied
3. Ice water
4. Man at nearby table keeps giving me disturbing/awesome look
5. Dinner cereal</review><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None</Resp><gmap_id>0x8085735268d0a2e7:0x122d343d99af9be</gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
